   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Assumption of Mary</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       The bodily taking up of the Virgin Mary into Heaven at the end of her earthly life
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Assunta" redirects here. For the hospital in Malaysia, see <a href="/wiki/Assunta_Hospital" title="Assunta Hospital">Assunta Hospital</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Santa Maria Assunta" redirects here. For churches with this dedication, see <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Assunta_(churches)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Maria Assunta (churches)">Santa Maria Assunta (churches)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Saint Mary of the Assumption" redirects here. For cathedrals with this dedication, see <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary_of_the_Assumption_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Cathedral of Saint Mary of the Assumption (disambiguation)">Cathedral of Saint Mary of the Assumption</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the theological concept. For works of art with this title, see <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_the_Virgin_Mary_in_art" title="Assumption of the Virgin Mary in art">Assumption of the Virgin Mary in art</a>.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p>

      <p>The <b>Assumption of Mary</b> (name in full <b>Assumption of the Blessed Virgin Mary</b>) is, according to the beliefs of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Churches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodoxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_East" title="Church of the East">Church of the East</a>, and some <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Catholicism" title="Anglo-Catholicism">Anglo-Catholic</a> Churches, among others, the <a href="/wiki/Entering_heaven_alive" title="Entering heaven alive">bodily taking up</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">Mary, the mother of Jesus</a>, into <a href="/wiki/Heaven_(Christianity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heaven (Christianity)">Heaven</a> at the end of her earthly life. The analogous feast in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Churches">Eastern Churches</a> is known as the <a href="/wiki/Dormition_of_the_Theotokos" class="mw-redirect" title="Dormition of the Theotokos">Dormition of the Theotokos</a>. </p>
      <p>In the churches that observe it, the Assumption is a major <a href="/wiki/Feast_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Feast day">feast day</a>, commonly celebrated on 15 August. In many countries, the feast is also marked as a <a href="/wiki/Holy_Day_of_Obligation" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Day of Obligation">Holy Day of Obligation</a> in the Catholic Church. The <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_the_Virgin_Mary_in_art" title="Assumption of the Virgin Mary in art">Assumption of the Virgin Mary in art</a> has been a popular subject, especially since the 12th century. </p>
      <p>The Catholic Church teaches as <a href="/wiki/Dogma_(Roman_Catholic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogma (Roman Catholic)">dogma</a> that the Virgin Mary "having completed the course of her earthly life, was assumed body and soul into heavenly glory".<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> This doctrine was <a href="/wiki/Dogmatic_definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogmatic definition">dogmatically defined</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pope Pius XII</a> on 1 November 1950, in the apostolic constitution <i><a href="/wiki/Munificentissimus_Deus" title="Munificentissimus Deus">Munificentissimus Deus</a></i> by exercising <a href="/wiki/Papal_infallibility" title="Papal infallibility">papal infallibility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> While the Catholic Church and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> believe in the <a href="/wiki/Dormition_of_the_Mother_of_God" title="Dormition of the Mother of God">Dormition of the Mother of God</a> (Dormition of the Theotokos or "the Falling Asleep of the Mother of God"),<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> whether Mary had a physical death has not been dogmatically defined. In <i><a href="/wiki/Munificentissimus_Deus" title="Munificentissimus Deus">Munificentissimus Deus</a></i> (item 39) Pope Pius XII pointed to the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a> (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(American_Standard)/Genesis#3:15" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Bible (American Standard)/Genesis">3:15</a>) as scriptural support for the dogma in terms of Mary's victory over sin and death through her intimate association with "the new Adam" (Christ)<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> as also reflected in <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(American_Standard)/1_Corinthians#15:54" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Bible (American Standard)/1 Corinthians">1 Corinthians 15:54</a>: "then shall come to pass the saying that is written, Death is swallowed up in victory".<sup id="cite_ref-IntroM75_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IntroM75-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mariology_pages_328-350_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mariology_pages_328-350-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-item_39at_the_Vatican_web_site_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-item_39at_the_Vatican_web_site-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a> contains no explicit narrative about the death or dormition, nor of the Assumption of Mary, but several scriptural passages have been theologically interpreted to describe the ultimate fate in this and the afterworld of the Mother of Jesus (see <a href="#Scriptural_basis">below</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ARCIC_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARCIC-10">[10]</a></sup> Various <a href="/wiki/Apocryphal" class="mw-redirect" title="Apocryphal">apocryphal</a> documents do contain narrations of the event. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The word "assumption" comes from the Middle English "assumpcioun" which means "a taking up into heaven", and from Latin "assumptio" which means "a taking".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Doctrine">Doctrine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Doctrine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>In 1950 Pope <a href="/wiki/Pius_XII" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius XII">Pius XII</a> invoked <a href="/wiki/Papal_infallibility" title="Papal infallibility">papal infallibility</a> to define the dogma of the Assumption of the Blessed Virgin in his Apostolic Constitution <i><a href="/wiki/Munificentissimus_Deus" title="Munificentissimus Deus">Munificentissimus Deus</a></i>:<sup id="cite_ref-Resch2016_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resch2016-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nicolas_Poussin,_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin,_c._1630-1632,_NGA_46470.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Nicolas_Poussin%2C_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin%2C_c._1630-1632%2C_NGA_46470.jpg/220px-Nicolas_Poussin%2C_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin%2C_c._1630-1632%2C_NGA_46470.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="301" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Nicolas_Poussin%2C_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin%2C_c._1630-1632%2C_NGA_46470.jpg/330px-Nicolas_Poussin%2C_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin%2C_c._1630-1632%2C_NGA_46470.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Nicolas_Poussin%2C_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin%2C_c._1630-1632%2C_NGA_46470.jpg/440px-Nicolas_Poussin%2C_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin%2C_c._1630-1632%2C_NGA_46470.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2922" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nicolas_Poussin,_The_Assumption_of_the_Virgin,_c._1630-1632,_NGA_46470.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Poussin" title="Nicolas Poussin">Nicolas Poussin</a>, <i>The Assumption of the Virgin</i>, c. 1630-1632
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <blockquote> 
       <p>We proclaim and define it to be a dogma revealed by God that the immaculate Mother of God, Mary ever virgin, when the course of her earthly life was finished, was taken up body and soul into the glory of heaven.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinge201253_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinge201253-13">[13]</a></sup> </p> 
      </blockquote> 
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Munificentissimus_Deus" title="Munificentissimus Deus">Munificentissimus Deus</a></i> emphasised Mary's unity with her divine son and as his mother, she is the mother of his church which is his body; she is the "new Eve" (the term is used three times), paralleling Christ as the new Adam;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerr2001746_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerr2001746-14">[14]</a></sup> and by her assumption she has attained the final bodily resurrection promised to all Christians, and the Church has reached its ultimate salvation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinge201253_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinge201253-13">[13]</a></sup> These three plus the <a href="/wiki/Perpetual_Virginity_of_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Perpetual Virginity of Mary">Perpetual Virginity of Mary</a> make up the four <a href="/wiki/Marian_dogmas" class="mw-redirect" title="Marian dogmas">Marian dogmas</a> of the Catholic church. </p>
      <p>The dogma of the Assumption followed from the 1854 definition of Mary's <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a> (her freedom from <a href="/wiki/Original_sin" title="Original sin">original sin</a>) and both developed from the recognition of her status as the <a href="/wiki/Mother_of_God" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother of God">Mother of God</a>, meaning that she, like Jesus, was without sin, preserved from corruption, resurrected, received into heaven, and a recipient of corporeal glory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerr2001746_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerr2001746-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>In the late 4th century, <a href="/wiki/Epiphanius_of_Salamis" title="Epiphanius of Salamis">Epiphanius of Salamis</a> wrote of his search for reliable traditions concerning the fate of Mary and his inability to discover any.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200211-12_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200211-12-15">[15]</a></sup> His inquiry suggests that discussion of Mary's immortality had already arisen in popular circles, and he identifies three beliefs concerning her end: that she died a normal and peaceful death; that she died a martyr; and that she did not die.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200214_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200214-16">[16]</a></sup> He suggested tentatively that Chapter 12 of the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">Book of Revelation</a>, which speaks of a woman "clothed with the Sun" who escapes "the dragon" by fleeing into the wilderness to be nourished "for a time, and times, and half a time," might possibly be a reference to her immortality, but the early church identified the woman with the church and there is no evidence that an identification with Mary existed before Epiphanius.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200211-12_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200211-12-15">[15]</a></sup> "No one knows her end," he concludes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200214_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200214-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Dormition/Assumption of Mary makes its first appearance in two apocryphal texts from the third and fourth centuries, the <i>Liber Requiei Mariae</i> ("Book of Mary's Repose"), and the "Six Books Dormition Apocryphon".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker2006unpaginated_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker2006unpaginated-17">[17]</a></sup> Both come from heterodox (i.e., proto-heretical) circles, the first having strong <a href="/wiki/Gnostic" class="mw-redirect" title="Gnostic">Gnostic</a> overtones and the second associated with a sect called the Kollyridians, whom Epiphanius condemned for their excessive devotion to Mary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker2006unpaginated_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker2006unpaginated-17">[17]</a></sup> Notable later apocrypha based on these include <i>De Obitu S. Dominae</i> and <i>De Transitu Virginis</i>, both probably from the 5th century, with further versions by <a href="/wiki/Dionysius_the_Areopagite" title="Dionysius the Areopagite">Dionysius the Areopagite</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St_Gregory_of_Tours" class="mw-redirect" title="St Gregory of Tours">St Gregory of Tours</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZirpolo2018213_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZirpolo2018213-18">[18]</a></sup> The <i>Transitus Mariae</i> was among apocrypha condemned in a 6th-century work called <i>Decretum Gelasium</i> (the "Decree of <a href="/wiki/Gelasius_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Gelasius I">Gelasius</a>", although not in fact by Pope Galasius I),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200217_and_fn_27_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShoemaker200217_and_fn_27-19">[19]</a></sup> but by the early 8th century it was so well established that <a href="/wiki/John_of_Damascus" title="John of Damascus">John of Damascus</a> could set out what had become the standard Eastern tradition, that "Mary died in the presence of the Apostles, but that her tomb, when opened, upon the request of St Thomas, was found empty; wherefrom the Apostles concluded that the body was taken up to heaven."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJenkins2015unpaginated_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJenkins2015unpaginated-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_(Parma)_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Cathedral_%28Parma%29_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg/220px-Cathedral_%28Parma%29_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Cathedral_%28Parma%29_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg/330px-Cathedral_%28Parma%29_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Cathedral_%28Parma%29_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg/440px-Cathedral_%28Parma%29_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3550" data-file-height="2936"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_(Parma)_-_Assumption_by_Correggio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_the_Virgin_(Correggio)" title="Assumption of the Virgin (Correggio)">Parma Cathedral, illusionistic dome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_da_Correggio" title="Antonio da Correggio">Correggio</a>, 1526-30
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In some versions of the story, the event is said to have taken place in <a href="/wiki/Ephesus" title="Ephesus">Ephesus</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_Virgin_Mary" title="House of the Virgin Mary">House of the Virgin Mary</a>. This is a much more recent and localized tradition. The earliest traditions say that Mary's life ended in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> (see "<a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Virgin_Mary" title="Tomb of the Virgin Mary">Mary's Tomb</a>"). By the 7th century, a variation emerged, according to which one of the apostles, often identified as <a href="/wiki/Thomas_the_Apostle" title="Thomas the Apostle">St Thomas</a>, was not present at the death of Mary but his late arrival precipitates a reopening of Mary's tomb, which is found to be empty except for her grave clothes. In a later tradition, Mary drops <a href="/wiki/Girdle_of_Thomas" title="Girdle of Thomas">her girdle</a> down to the apostle from heaven as testament to the event.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> This incident is depicted in many later paintings of the Assumption. </p>
      <p>Teaching of the Assumption of Mary became widespread across the Christian world, having been celebrated as early as the 5th century and having been established in the East by Emperor Maurice around AD 600.<sup id="cite_ref-Alban140_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alban140-22">[22]</a></sup> St. John Damascene records the following: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>St. Juvenal, Bishop of Jerusalem, at the Council of Chalcedon (451), made known to the Emperor Marcian and Pulcheria, who wished to possess the body of the Mother of God, that Mary died in the presence of all the Apostles, but that her tomb, when opened upon the request of St. Thomas, was found empty; wherefrom the Apostles concluded that the body was taken up to heaven.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>The Assumption of Mary was celebrated in the West under <a href="/wiki/Pope_Sergius_I" title="Pope Sergius I">Pope Sergius I</a> in the 8th century and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_IV" title="Pope Leo IV">Pope Leo IV</a> confirmed the feast as official.<sup id="cite_ref-Alban140_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alban140-22">[22]</a></sup> Theological debate about the Assumption continued, following the Reformation. But the people celebrated the Assumption as part of the cult of Mary that flourished from the Middle Ages.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="no link or previous mention of">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1950 Pope <a href="/wiki/Pius_XII" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius XII">Pius XII</a> defined it as dogma for the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vatican-deus_en_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vatican-deus_en-24">[24]</a></sup> Catholic theologian <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Ott" title="Ludwig Ott">Ludwig Ott</a> stated, "The idea of the bodily assumption of Mary is first expressed in certain transitus-narratives of the fifth and sixth centuries.&nbsp;... The first Church author to speak of the bodily assumption of Mary, in association with an apocryphal transitus of the <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus#In_Christianity" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">B.M.V.</a>, is St. Gregory of Tours."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> writer <a href="/wiki/Eamon_Duffy" title="Eamon Duffy">Eamon Duffy</a> states that "there is, clearly, no historical evidence whatever for it."<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> However, the Catholic Church has never asserted nor denied that its teaching is based on the apocryphal accounts.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="asserting a response to an inquiry without evidence of the inquiry (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Church documents are silent on this matter and instead rely upon other sources and arguments as the basis for the doctrine.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Silent documents are not specified and">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Catholic_teaching">Catholic teaching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Catholic teaching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1013635363">.mw-parser-output .sidebar{width:22em;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 1em;background:#f8f9fa;border:1px solid          <td class="sidebar-content hlist"> 
          <div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed">
           <div class="sidebar-list-title" style="text-align:center; background-color:gold">
            <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Marian_movements_and_societies" title="Catholic Marian movements and societies">Movements and societies</a>
           </div>
           <div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content"> 
            <ul>
             <li><a href="/wiki/Sodality_of_Our_Lady" title="Sodality of Our Lady">Sodality of Our Lady</a></li> 
             <li><a href="/wiki/Congregation_of_Marian_Fathers_of_the_Immaculate_Conception" title="Congregation of Marian Fathers of the Immaculate Conception">Congregation of Marian Fathers</a></li> 
             <li><a href="/wiki/Company_of_Mary" title="Company of Mary">Company of Mary (Montfort)</a></li> 
             <li><a href="/wiki/Society_of_Mary_(Marianists)" title="Society of Mary (Marianists)">Marianists (Society of Mary)</a></li> 
             <li><a href="/wiki/Society_of_Mary_(Marists)" title="Society of Mary (Marists)">Marist Fathers</a></li>

             <li><a href="/wiki/Blue_Army_of_Our_Lady_of_F%C3%A1tima" title="Blue Army of Our Lady of Fátima">World Apostolate of Fátima</a> <a href="/wiki/Blue_Army_of_Our_Lady_of_F%C3%A1tima" title="Blue Army of Our Lady of Fátima">(Blue Army)</a></li>

            </ul>
           </div>
          </div></td> 
        </tr>

         <td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style>

           <ul>
            <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Catholic_Mariology_sidebar" title="Template:Catholic Mariology sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>

            <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Catholic_Mariology_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>

      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theological_issues">Theological issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Theological issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Pius XII's dogmatic statement, the phrase "having completed the course of her earthly life", leaves open the question of whether the Virgin Mary died before her assumption or not. Mary's assumption is said to have been a divine gift to her as the 'Mother of God'. Ludwig Ott's view is that, as Mary completed her life as a shining example to the human race, the perspective of the gift of assumption is offered to the whole human race.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ludwig Ott writes in his book <i>Fundamentals of Catholic Dogma</i> that "the fact of her death is almost generally accepted by the Fathers and Theologians, and is expressly affirmed in the Liturgy of the Church", to which he adds a number of helpful citations. He concludes: "for Mary, death, in consequence of her freedom from <a href="/wiki/Original_sin" title="Original sin">original sin</a> and from personal sin, was not a consequence of punishment of sin. However, it seems fitting that Mary's body, which was by nature mortal, should be, in conformity with that of her <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Divine Son</a>, subject to the general law of death".<sup id="cite_ref-Ott6_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ott6-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The point of her bodily death has not been infallibly defined by any pope. Many Catholics believe that she did not die at all, but was assumed directly into Heaven. The dogmatic definition within the Apostolic Constitution <i><a href="/wiki/Munificentissimus_Deus" title="Munificentissimus Deus">Munificentissimus Deus</a></i> which, according to Roman Catholic dogma, infallibly proclaims the doctrine of the Assumption leaves open the question of whether, in connection with her departure, Mary underwent bodily death. It does not dogmatically define the point one way or the other, as shown by the words "having completed the course of her earthly life".<sup id="cite_ref-Vatican-deus_en_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vatican-deus_en-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scriptural_basis">Scriptural basis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Scriptural basis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus#After_the_Ascension_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Mary, mother of Jesus §&nbsp;After the Ascension of Jesus</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Munificentissimus_Deus" title="Munificentissimus Deus">Munificentissimus Deus</a></i>, near the end of the review of the doctrine's history, Pope <a href="/wiki/Pius_XII" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius XII">Pius XII</a> stated: "All these proofs and considerations of the holy Fathers and the theologians are based upon the Sacred Writings as their ultimate foundation." Precedent to this, he cited many passages that have been offered in support of this teaching. </p>
      <p>The pope cited <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=1+Corinthians+15&amp;version=NRSV">1 Corinthians 15</a></span>. In this passage Paul alludes to <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Genesis+3%3A15&amp;version=NRSV">Genesis 3:15</a></span> (in addition to the primary reference of <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Psalm+8%3A6&amp;version=NRSV">Psalm 8:6</a></span>), where it is prophesied that the <a href="/wiki/Seed_of_the_woman" title="Seed of the woman">seed of the woman</a> will crush Satan with his feet: "I will put enmities between thee and the woman, and thy seed and her seed: she shall crush thy head, and thou shalt lie in wait for her heel." Since then, Jesus arose to Heaven to fulfill this prophecy, it follows that the woman would have a similar end since she shared this enmity with Satan. </p>
      <p>The pope also mentioned (in paragraph 26) <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Psalm+132&amp;version=NRSV">Psalm 132</a></span>, a psalm commemorating the return of the <a href="/wiki/Ark_of_the_Covenant" title="Ark of the Covenant">Ark of God</a> to Jerusalem and lamenting its subsequent loss. The second half of the psalm says that the loss will be recompensed in the New Covenant, and so it is hopefully prayed, "Arise, O Lord, into thy resting place: thou and the ark, which thou hast sanctified" (v. 8). Since the Church sees this New Covenant ark in Mary, it understands that she was taken into Heaven in the same manner as the Lord – that is, body and soul. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rotunda_Church.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Rotunda_Church.jpg/220px-Rotunda_Church.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Rotunda_Church.jpg/330px-Rotunda_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Rotunda_Church.jpg/440px-Rotunda_Church.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rotunda_Church.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Basilica of the Assumption of Our Lady in Mosta, Malta. The church is also known as Mosta Dome or as Mosta Rotunda. The façade of the Basilica is decorated for the feast of the Assumption which is annually celebrated on the 15th of August.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Finally, he mentioned in the next paragraph "that woman clothed with the sun [<span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Revelation+12%3A1%E2%80%932&amp;version=NRSV">Revelation 12:1–2</a></span>] whom John the Apostle contemplated on the Island of Patmos" was support for the defining of this dogmatic doctrine for Catholics. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assumption_versus_Dormition">Assumption versus Dormition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Assumption versus Dormition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Dormition_of_the_Mother_of_God" title="Dormition of the Mother of God">Dormition of the Mother of God</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG/220px-Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG/330px-Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG/440px-Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1335" data-file-height="1473"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Dormition: ivory plaque, late 10th-early 11th century (<a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_Cluny" title="Musée de Cluny">Musée de Cluny</a>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many Catholics believe that Mary first died before being assumed, but they believe that she was miraculously resurrected before being assumed. Others believe she was assumed bodily into Heaven without first dying.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Either understanding may be legitimately held by Catholics, with <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholics</a> observing the Feast as the Dormition. </p>
      <p>Many theologians note by way of comparison that in the Catholic Church the Assumption is dogmatically defined, whilst in the Eastern Orthodox tradition the Dormition is less dogmatically than liturgically and mystically defined. Such differences spring from a larger pattern in the two traditions, wherein Catholic teachings are often dogmatically and authoritatively defined – in part because of the more centralized structure of the Catholic Church – whilst in Eastern Orthodoxy many doctrines are less authoritative.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Latin_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin Catholic">Latin Catholic</a> Feast of the Assumption is celebrated on 15 August and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Catholics">Eastern Catholics</a> celebrate the Dormition of the Mother of God (or Dormition of the Theotokos, the falling asleep of the Mother of God) on the same date, preceded by a 14-day <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">fast</a> period. Eastern Christians believe that Mary died a natural death, that her soul was received by Christ upon death, that her body was resurrected on the third day after her death and that she was taken up into heaven bodily in anticipation of the general <a href="/wiki/Resurrection" title="Resurrection">resurrection</a>. </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942">
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>Orthodox tradition is clear and unwavering in regard to the central point [of the Dormition]: the Holy Virgin underwent, as did her Son, a physical death, but her body – like His – was afterwards raised from the dead and she was taken up into heaven, in her body as well as in her soul. She has passed beyond death and judgement and lives wholly in the Age to Come. The Resurrection of the Body ... has in her case been anticipated and is already an accomplished fact. That does not mean, however, that she is dissociated from the rest of humanity and placed in a wholly different category: for we all hope to share one day in that same glory of the Resurrection of the Body that she enjoys even now.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestant_views">Protestant views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Protestant views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rubens,_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_(Antwerpen).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Rubens%2C_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_%28Antwerpen%29.jpg/220px-Rubens%2C_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_%28Antwerpen%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Rubens%2C_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_%28Antwerpen%29.jpg/330px-Rubens%2C_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_%28Antwerpen%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Rubens%2C_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_%28Antwerpen%29.jpg/440px-Rubens%2C_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_%28Antwerpen%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3239" data-file-height="4800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rubens,_Mari%C3%A4_Himmelfahrt_(Antwerpen).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>The Assumption of Mary</i>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Rubens</a>, 1626
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Views differ within Protestantism, with those with a theology closer to Catholicism sometimes believing in a bodily assumption whilst most Protestants do not. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglican_views">Anglican views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Anglican views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Within <a href="/wiki/Anglican_doctrine" title="Anglican doctrine">Anglican doctrine</a> the Assumption of Mary is either rejected or regarded as <a href="/wiki/Adiaphora" title="Adiaphora">adiaphora</a> ("a thing indifferent");<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> it therefore disappeared from Anglican worship in 1549, partially returning in some branches of Anglicanism during the 20th century under different names. A Marian feast on 15 August is celebrated by the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> as a non-specific <a href="/wiki/Festival_(Anglicanism)" title="Festival (Anglicanism)">feast</a> of the Blessed Virgin Mary, a feast called by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Scottish Episcopal Church</a> simply "Mary the Virgin",<sup id="cite_ref-Williams,_Paul_2007_p._253_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Paul_2007_p._253-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and in the US-based <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal Church</a> it is observed as the feast of "Saint Mary the Virgin: Mother of Our Lord Jesus Christ",<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> while other Anglican provinces have a feast of the Dormition<sup id="cite_ref-Williams,_Paul_2007_p._253_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Paul_2007_p._253-34">[34]</a></sup> – the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Canada" title="Anglican Church of Canada">Anglican Church of Canada</a> for instance marks the day as the "Falling Asleep of the Blessed Virgin Mary",<sup id="cite_ref-PrayerBook_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrayerBook-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Anglican-Roman_Catholic_International_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican-Roman Catholic International Commission">Anglican-Roman Catholic International Commission</a>, which seeks to identify common ground between the two communions, released in 2004 a non-authoritative declaration meant for study and evaluation, the "Seattle Statement"; this "agreed statement" concludes that "the teaching about Mary in the two definitions of the Assumption and the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>, understood within the biblical pattern of the economy of hope and grace, can be said to be consonant with the teaching of the Scriptures and the ancient common traditions".<sup id="cite_ref-ARCIC_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARCIC-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Protestant_views">Other Protestant views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other Protestant views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Protestant Reformer <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Bullinger" title="Heinrich Bullinger">Heinrich Bullinger</a> believed in the assumption of Mary. His 1539 polemical treatise against idolatry<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> expressed his belief that Mary's <i>sacrosanctum corpus</i> ("sacrosanct body") had been assumed into heaven by angels: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942">
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p><i>Hac causa credimus ut Deiparae virginis Mariae purissimum thalamum et spiritus sancti templum, hoc est, sacrosanctum corpus ejus deportatum esse ab angelis in coelum.</i><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> For this reason we believe that the Virgin Mary, Begetter of God, the most pure bed and temple of the Holy Spirit, that is, her most holy body, was carried to heaven by angels.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>Most modern Protestants neither teach nor believe in the Assumption of Mary, since they see no <a href="/wiki/Sola_Scriptura" class="mw-redirect" title="Sola Scriptura">biblical basis</a> or extra-biblical basis for it. Although many churches within <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> do not teach the Assumption of Mary, 15 August remains a Lesser Feast in celebration of "Mary, Mother of Our Lord", according to the <a href="/wiki/Calendar_of_Saints_(Lutheran)" class="mw-redirect" title="Calendar of Saints (Lutheran)">Calendar of Saints</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feasts">Feasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Feasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg/220px-Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg/330px-Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg/440px-Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Assunzione_agosto_NovaradiSicilia_tre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The feast of the Assumption of the Virgin Mary at <a href="/wiki/Novara_di_Sicilia" title="Novara di Sicilia">Novara di Sicilia</a> in August
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Assumption is important to many Catholic and Eastern Orthodox Christians as the Virgin Mary's heavenly birthday (the day that Mary was received into Heaven). Belief about her acceptance into the glory of Heaven is seen by some Christians as the symbol of the promise made by Jesus to all enduring Christians that they too will be received into paradise. The Assumption of Mary is symbolised in the <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lys" class="mw-redirect" title="Fleur-de-lys">Fleur-de-lys</a> Madonna. </p>
      <p>The present Italian name of the holiday, <i>"<a href="/wiki/Ferragosto" title="Ferragosto">Ferragosto</a>"</i>, may derive from the Latin name, <i>Feriae Augusti</i> ("Holidays of the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Augustus" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor Augustus">Emperor Augustus</a>"),<sup id="cite_ref-Pianigiani_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pianigiani-43">[43]</a></sup> since the month of August took its name from the emperor. The Solemnity of the Assumption on 15 August was celebrated in the Eastern Church from the 6th Century. The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> adopted this date as a <a href="/wiki/Holy_Day_of_Obligation" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Day of Obligation">Holy Day of Obligation</a> to commemorate the Assumption of the <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Blessed Virgin Mary">Blessed Virgin Mary</a>, a reference to the belief in a real, physical elevation of her sinless soul and incorrupt body into Heaven. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg/220px-Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg/330px-Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg/440px-Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4597" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Goan_style_Patoleo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>'<a href="/wiki/Patoleo" title="Patoleo">Patoleo</a>' (sweet rice cakes) are the <i>Pièce de résistance</i> of the Assumption feast celebration among <a href="/wiki/Goan_Catholics" title="Goan Catholics">Goan Catholics</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Assumption+of+Mary%22">"Assumption of Mary"</a>&nbsp;–&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Assumption+of+Mary%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Assumption+of+Mary%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Assumption+of+Mary%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Assumption+of+Mary%22">scholar</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Assumption+of+Mary%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Assumption Day on 15 August is a nationwide public holiday in Andorra, Austria, Belgium, Burundi, Cameroon, Central African Republic, Chile, Republic of Congo, Côte d'Ivoire, Croatia, Colombia, Costa Rica, Cyprus, East Timor, France, Gabon, Greece, Georgia, Republic of Guinea, Haiti, Italy, Lebanon, Lithuania, Luxembourg, Republic of North Macedonia, Madagascar, Malta, Mauritius, Republic of Moldova, Monaco, Montenegro (Albanian Catholics), Paraguay, Poland (coinciding with Polish Army Day), Portugal, Romania, Rwanda, Senegal, Seychelles, Slovenia, Spain, Syria, Tahiti, Togo, and Vanuatu;<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-44">[44]</a></sup> and was also in <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> until <a href="/wiki/1948" title="1948">1948</a>. </p>
      <p>It is also a public holiday in parts of Germany (parts of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">Saarland</a>) and Switzerland (in 14 of the 26 <a href="/wiki/Swiss_canton" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss canton">cantons</a>). In Guatemala, it is observed in <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">Guatemala City</a> and in the town of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Nebaj" title="Santa Maria Nebaj">Santa Maria Nebaj</a>, both of which claim her as their <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Also, this day is combined with <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day" title="Mother's Day">Mother's Day</a> in Costa Rica and parts of Belgium. </p>
      <p>Prominent Catholic, Eastern Orthodox, and Oriental Orthodox countries in which Assumption Day is an important festival but is not recognized by the state as a public holiday include the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, the Feast of the Assumption is the biggest Eastern Orthodox Christian celebration of the Holy Virgin. Celebrations include liturgies and votive offerings. In Varna, the day is celebrated with a procession of a holy icon, and with concerts and regattas.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Assumption_Mosta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Assumption_Mosta.jpg/220px-Assumption_Mosta.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Assumption_Mosta.jpg/330px-Assumption_Mosta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Assumption_Mosta.jpg/440px-Assumption_Mosta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Assumption_Mosta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Titular statue of the Assumption of Our Lady located in the <a href="/wiki/Rotunda_of_Mosta" title="Rotunda of Mosta">Basilica of the Assumption of Our Lady</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mosta" title="Mosta">Mosta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>. The statue was crafted by Salvatore Dimech in 1868 and remodelled in 1947 by Vincent Apap.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In many places, religious parades and popular festivals are held to celebrate this day. In Canada, Assumption Day is the Fête Nationale of the <a href="/wiki/Acadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Acadian">Acadians</a>, of whom she is the patron saint. Some businesses close on that day in heavily francophone parts of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, Canada. The Virgin Assumed in Heaven is also patroness of the <a href="/wiki/Maltese_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Maltese Islands">Maltese Islands</a> and her feast, celebrated on 15 August, apart from being a public holiday in Malta is also celebrated with great solemnity in the local churches especially in the seven localities known as the Seba' Santa Marijiet. The Maltese localities which celebrate the Assumption of Our Lady are: Il-<a href="/wiki/Mosta" title="Mosta">Mosta</a>, Il-<a href="/wiki/Qrendi" title="Qrendi">Qrendi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirkop" title="Kirkop">Ħal-Kirkop</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hal-Ghaxaq&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hal-Ghaxaq (page does not exist)">Hal-Ghaxaq</a>, Il-<a href="/wiki/Gudja" title="Gudja">Gudja</a>, Ħ' <a href="/wiki/Attard" title="Attard">Attard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mqabba" title="Mqabba">L-Imqabba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Gozo" title="Victoria, Gozo">Victoria</a>. The hamlet of <a href="/wiki/Praha,_Texas" title="Praha, Texas">Praha, Texas</a> holds a festival during which its population swells from approximately 25 to 5,000 people. </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a>, the feast is now often kept, but without official use of the word "Assumption". In Eastern Orthodox churches following the <a href="/wiki/Julian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian Calendar">Julian Calendar</a>, the feast day of Assumption of Mary falls on 28 August. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_the_Virgin_Mary_in_art" title="Assumption of the Virgin Mary in art">Assumption of the Virgin Mary in art</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The earliest known use of the Dormition is found on a sarcophagus in the crypt of a church in <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">Zaragoza</a> in Spain dated c.330.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZirpolo2018213_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZirpolo2018213-18">[18]</a></sup> The Assumption became a popular subject in Western Christian art, especially from the 12th century, and especially after the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a>, when it was used to refute the Protestants and their downplaying of Mary's role in salvation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZirpolo201883_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZirpolo201883-47">[47]</a></sup> Angels commonly carry her heavenward where she is to be crowned by Christ, while the Apostles below surround her empty tomb as they stare up in awe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZirpolo201883_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZirpolo201883-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Caravaggio" title="Caravaggio">Caravaggio</a>, the "father" of the <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> movement, caused a stir by depicting her as a decaying corpse, quite contrary to the doctrine promoted by the Church;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZirpolo2018213-214_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZirpolo2018213-214-48">[48]</a></sup> more orthodox examples include works by <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">El Greco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rubens" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubens">Rubens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annibale_Caracci" class="mw-redirect" title="Annibale Caracci">Annibale Caracci</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Poussin" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas Poussin">Nicholas Poussin</a>, the last replacing the Apostles with <a href="/wiki/Putti" class="mw-redirect" title="Putti">putti</a> throwing flowers into the tomb.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZirpolo201883_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZirpolo201883-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Assumption_of_Mary&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

         <li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Encyclopedia of Catholicism</i> by Frank K. Flinn, J. Gordon Melton 207 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-8160-5455-X" title="Special:BookSources/0-8160-5455-X">0-8160-5455-X</a> p. 267</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.vatican.va/holy_father/pius_xii/apost_constitutions/documents/hf_p-xii_apc_19501101_munificentissimus-deus_en.html">Munificentissimus Deus, 17</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130904181017/https://www.vatican.va/holy_father/pius_xii/apost_constitutions/documents/hf_p-xii_apc_19501101_munificentissimus-deus_en.html">Archived</a> 4 September 2013 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> In the liturgical books which deal with the feast either of the dormition or of the Assumption of the Blessed Virgin there are expressions that agree in testifying that, when the Virgin Mother of God passed from this earthly exile to heaven, what happened to her sacred body was, by the decree of divine Providence, in keeping with the dignity of the Mother of the Word Incarnate, and with the other privileges she had been accorded.</span> </li>

"In the <i>De origine erroris in divorum ac simulachrorum cultu</i> he opposed the worship of the saints and iconolatry; in the <i>De origine erroris in negocio Eucharistiae ac Missae</i> he strove to show that the Catholic conceptions of the Eucharist and of celebrating the Mass were wrong. Bullinger published a combined edition of these works in <a href="/wiki/Octavo" title="Octavo">4 °</a> (Zurich 1539), which was divided into two books, according to themes of the original work." <i>The Library of the Finnish nobleman, royal secretary and trustee Henrik Matsson (c. 1540–1617)</i>, Terhi Kiiskinen Helsinki: Academia Scientarium Fennica (Finnish Academy of Science), 2003, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/951-41-0944-9" title="Special:BookSources/951-41-0944-9">951-41-0944-9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9789514109447" title="Special:BookSources/9789514109447">9789514109447</a>, p. 175 <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.google.com/search?q=%22he+opposed+the+worship+of+the+saints+and+iconolatry%22&amp;hl=en&amp;client=firefox-a&amp;hs=WVr&amp;rls=org.mozilla%3Aen-US%3Aofficial&amp;num=10&amp;lr=&amp;ft=i&amp;cr=&amp;safe=images&amp;tbs=#q=%22he+opposed+the+worship+of+the+saints+and+iconolatry%22&amp;hl=en&amp;client=firefox-a&amp;hs=WVr&amp;rls=org.mozilla:en-US:official&amp;num=10&amp;lr=&amp;ft=i&amp;cr=&amp;safe=images&amp;um=1&amp;ie=UTF-8&amp;tbo=u&amp;tbs=,bks:1&amp;source=og&amp;sa=N&amp;tab=wp&amp;fp=e0e76270dccd6427">[3]</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Froschauer. <i>De origine erroris</i>, Caput XVI (Chapter 16), p. 70</span> </li>

      <ul>
       <li>Duggan, Paul E. (1989). <i>The Assumption Dogma: Some Reactions and Ecumenical Implications in the Thought of English-speaking Theologians</i>. Emerson Press, Cleveland, Ohio.</li> 
       <li>Mimouni, Simon Claude (1995). <i>Dormition et assomption de Marie: Histoire des traditions anciennes</i>. Beauchesne, Paris.</li> 
       <li>
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFSalvador-Gonzalez2019" class="citation journal cs1">Salvador-Gonzalez, José-María (2019).
